With `OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD`, the first call adds or overwrites the header, and the second call overwrites it again.\n\nThe task description shows duplicates even with `OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD`, suggesting either the formatter generates different values on each call or another mechanism is at play. The `encodeHeaders` method in filter_manager.cc iterates through encoder filters in reverse order compared to decoder filters. The duplication appears specific to LOCAL REPLIES rather than UPSTREAM RESPONSES, which points to a difference in how these response types flow through the filter chain.\n\nFor upstream responses, `modify_headers_` is passed to the connection and called once when the response arrives. For local replies, `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain` creates a lambda that invokes both `finalizeResponseHeaders()` directly and through `modify_headers_()`, causing the header modification to execute twice. The router filter's `sendLocalReply` call doesn't account for the fact that the filter manager's lambda already handles header finalization, leading to the duplicate application of the header `HeaderValueOption` message (lines 429-481) - Proto definition for route response header configuration\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Response headers configured via `response_headers_to_add` appear twice in HTTP responses for local replies (e.g., `x-custom-trace: abc123\\r\\nx-custom-trace: abc123`)\n\n2. **Access Log Evidence**: The `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` formatter shows responses like `upstream_response_timeout` with duplicate headers present in the actual HTTP response\n\n3. **Router Filter Initialization** (router.cc:444-461):\n   - Router filter creates `modify_headers_` callback during `decodeHeaders()`\n   - This callback includes a call to `route_entry_->finalizeResponseHeaders()` on line 453\n   - Designed to apply all route-level response header transformations\n\n4. **Local Error Detection** (router.cc:520-525, etc.):\n   - Router filter detects a local error condition (e.g., cluster not found)\n   - Calls `callbacks_->sendLocalReply(code, \"\", modify_headers_, ...)`\n   - Passes the `modify_headers_` callback to filter manager\n\n5. **Filter Manager Local Reply Path** (filter_manager.cc:1109-1140):\n   - `DownstreamFilterManager::sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` receives the `modify_headers_` callback\n   - Creates a new lambda that:\n     - Calls `finalizeResponseHeaders()` directly (line 1125)\n     - Calls the passed `modify_headers_` callback (line 1128)\n\n6. **Lack of Awareness of Redundancy** (filter_manager.cc:1072-1078, 1156-1162):\n   - Filter manager code pattern repeated identically in three methods: `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, `prepareLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, `sendDirectLocalReply()`\n   - Code does not account for the fact that `modify_headers_` already contains a `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call\n   - No guard to prevent double-finalization\n\n7. **Lambda Invocation** (utility.cc:719):\n   - `Utility::prepareLocalReply()` invokes the filter manager's lambda on response headers\n   - Both `finalizeResponseHeaders()` calls execute:\n     - First explicit call modifies headers\n     - Second implicit call (via `modify_headers_`) modifies headers again\n\n8. **Header Addition Mechanism** (header_parser.cc:182-212):\n   - For each configured header to add, `evaluateHeaders()` processes it according to its `append_action`\n   - First call: Header is added to response\n   - Second call: Header is processed again:\n     - If `APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD`: Header is APPENDED (creating duplicate)\n     - If `OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD`: Header is OVERWRITTEN (inefficient but no visible duplication if value is identical)\n     - If `ADD_IF_ABSENT`: Header is NOT added (no duplication)\n     - If `OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS`: Header is OVERWRITTEN (inefficient but no visible duplication)\n\n9. **Root Cause**: The filter manager's local reply construction unconditionally calls `finalizeResponseHeaders()` AND then calls `modify_headers_`, without recognizing that the router filter has already embedded `finalizeResponseHeaders()` within the `modify_headers_` callback\n\n10. **Contrast with Upstream Path** (router.cc:1794):\n    - For upstream responses, router calls `modify_headers_(*headers)` directly\n    - Upstream connection code does NOT wrap this with another `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call\n    - Result: Upstream responses receive headers exactly once\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Cause Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix should eliminate the double `finalizeResponseHeaders()` invocation. Two approaches:\n\n**Option A: Remove duplicate call in filter_manager.cc**\n- Modify the lambda creation in `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, `prepareLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, and `sendDirectLocalReply()`\n- Remove the direct `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call since `modify_headers_` already contains it\n- Relies on router filter always passing a `modify_headers_` callback that includes finalization\n- Risk: Other callers of `sendLocalReply()` that don't pass `modify_headers_` would skip finalization\n\n**Option B: Remove finalization from router.cc's modify_headers_**\n- Move the `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call out of the `modify_headers_` callback in router.cc\n- Call `finalizeResponseHeaders()` explicitly for upstream responses (after line 1794)\n- Allow filter manager to handle finalization for all cases\n- More centralized, but requires changes in router filter's upstream path handling\n\n**Option C: Add guard in filter_manager.cc**\n- Check if `modify_headers_` already performs finalization\n- Only call `finalizeResponseHeaders()` if needed\n- Most defensive but harder to implement and maintain\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Enable debug logging in router.cc to track when `modify_headers_` is created and called\n2. Add instrumentation in `evaluateHeaders()` (header_parser.cc) to log each call to `finalizeResponseHeaders()`\n3. Check response headers in access logs before and after each finalization step\n4. Verify that upstream responses (non-local replies) only show headers once\n\n### Testing Requirements\n\n- Add integration tests for local replies (timeout, cluster not found, overloaded) with `response_headers_to_add` configured\n- Verify headers appear exactly once with all `append_action` values: APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD, ADD_IF_ABSENT, OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD, OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS\n- Verify upstream responses still work correctly after fix\n- Verify gRPC local replies don't break\n- Verify direct local replies (when response headers already started) don't duplicate headers\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2087,"cache_read_input_tokens":60593,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2087},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"75353ff2-5bef-4fac-af44-ea55a1dee653","uuid":"bf1a3f36-5ff6-4cba-8eb6-19f44f3cd270"}

Duplicate header added in the `HeaderMap` for other headers.\"\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **source/common/router/router.cc**\n   - `Filter::decodeHeaders()` (line 444-461) - Creates `modify_headers_` callback with `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call\n   - Local reply invocations (lines 522, 550, 750, 931, 1004, 1060, 1340)\n\n2. **source/common/http/filter_manager.cc**\n   - `DownstreamFilterManager::sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` (lines 1109-1140) - Creates duplicate finalization lambda\n   - `DownstreamFilterManager::prepareLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` (lines 1055-1094) - Creates duplicate finalization lambda\n   - `DownstreamFilterManager::sendDirectLocalReply()` (lines 1147-1190) - Creates duplicate finalization lambda\n\n3. **source/common/http/utility.cc**\n   - `Utility::prepareLocalReply()` (lines 709-781) - Invokes the problematic lambda\n   - `Utility::sendLocalReply()` (lines 807-815) - Orchestrates local reply execution\n\n4. **source/common/router/config_impl.cc**\n   - `RouteEntryImplBase::finalizeResponseHeaders()` (lines 942-950) - Applies response header transformations\n\n5. **source/common/router/header_parser.cc**\n   - `HeadersToAddEntry` constructor (lines 53-76) - Parses `append_action` field\n   - `HeaderParser::evaluateHeaders()` (lines 139-213) - Evaluates and applies headers based on `append_action`\n\n6. **api/envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto**\n   - `HeaderValueOption` message (lines 429-481) - Proto definition for route response header configuration\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Response headers configured via `response_headers_to_add` appear twice in HTTP responses for local replies (e.g., `x-custom-trace: abc123\\r\\nx-custom-trace: abc123`)\n\n2. **Access Log Evidence**: The `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` formatter shows responses like `upstream_response_timeout` with duplicate headers present in the actual HTTP response\n\n3. **Router Filter Initialization** (router.cc:444-461):\n   - Router filter creates `modify_headers_` callback during `decodeHeaders()`\n   - This callback includes a call to `route_entry_->finalizeResponseHeaders()` on line 453\n   - Designed to apply all route-level response header transformations\n\n4. **Local Error Detection** (router.cc:520-525, etc.):\n   - Router filter detects a local error condition (e.g., cluster not found)\n   - Calls `callbacks_->sendLocalReply(code, \"\", modify_headers_, ...)`\n   - Passes the `modify_headers_` callback to filter manager\n\n5. **Filter Manager Local Reply Path** (filter_manager.cc:1109-1140):\n   - `DownstreamFilterManager::sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` receives the `modify_headers_` callback\n   - Creates a new lambda that:\n     - Calls `finalizeResponseHeaders()` directly (line 1125)\n     - Calls the passed `modify_headers_` callback (line 1128)\n\n6. **Lack of Awareness of Redundancy** (filter_manager.cc:1072-1078, 1156-1162):\n   - Filter manager code pattern repeated identically in three methods: `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, `prepareLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, `sendDirectLocalReply()`\n   - Code does not account for the fact that `modify_headers_` already contains a `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call\n   - No guard to prevent double-finalization\n\n7. **Lambda Invocation** (utility.cc:719):\n   - `Utility::prepareLocalReply()` invokes the filter manager's lambda on response headers\n   - Both `finalizeResponseHeaders()` calls execute:\n     - First explicit call modifies headers\n     - Second implicit call (via `modify_headers_`) modifies headers again\n\n8. **Header Addition Mechanism** (header_parser.cc:182-212):\n   - For each configured header to add, `evaluateHeaders()` processes it according to its `append_action`\n   - First call: Header is added to response\n   - Second call: Header is processed again:\n     - If `APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD`: Header is APPENDED (creating duplicate)\n     - If `OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD`: Header is OVERWRITTEN (inefficient but no visible duplication if value is identical)\n     - If `ADD_IF_ABSENT`: Header is NOT added (no duplication)\n     - If `OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS`: Header is OVERWRITTEN (inefficient but no visible duplication)\n\n9. **Root Cause**: The filter manager's local reply construction unconditionally calls `finalizeResponseHeaders()` AND then calls `modify_headers_`, without recognizing that the router filter has already embedded `finalizeResponseHeaders()` within the `modify_headers_` callback\n\n10. **Contrast with Upstream Path** (router.cc:1794):\n    - For upstream responses, router calls `modify_headers_(*headers)` directly\n    - Upstream connection code does NOT wrap this with another `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call\n    - Result: Upstream responses receive headers exactly once\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Cause Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix should eliminate the double `finalizeResponseHeaders()` invocation. Two approaches:\n\n**Option A: Remove duplicate call in filter_manager.cc**\n- Modify the lambda creation in `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, `prepareLocalReplyViaFilterChain()`, and `sendDirectLocalReply()`\n- Remove the direct `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call since `modify_headers_` already contains it\n- Relies on router filter always passing a `modify_headers_` callback that includes finalization\n- Risk: Other callers of `sendLocalReply()` that don't pass `modify_headers_` would skip finalization\n\n**Option B: Remove finalization from router.cc's modify_headers_**\n- Move the `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call out of the `modify_headers_` callback in router.cc\n- Call `finalizeResponseHeaders()` explicitly for upstream responses (after line 1794)\n- Allow filter manager to handle finalization for all cases\n- More centralized, but requires changes in router filter's upstream path handling\n\n**Option C: Add guard in filter_manager.cc**\n- Check if `modify_headers_` already performs finalization\n- Only call `finalizeResponseHeaders()` if needed\n- Most defensive but harder to implement and maintain\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Enable debug logging in router.cc to track when `modify_headers_` is created and called\n2. Add instrumentation in `evaluateHeaders()` (header_parser.cc) to log each call to `finalizeResponseHeaders()`\n3. Check response headers in access logs before and after each finalization step\n4. Verify that upstream responses (non-local replies) only show headers once\n\n### Testing Requirements\n\n- Add integration tests for local replies (timeout, cluster not found, overloaded) with `response_headers_to_add` configured\n- Verify headers appear exactly once with all `append_action` values: APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD, ADD_IF_ABSENT, OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD, OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS\n- Verify upstream responses still work correctly after fix\n- Verify gRPC local replies don't break\n- Verify direct local replies (when response headers already started) don't duplicate headers\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
